[PROJECT_MEMORY]

# Project Architecture & Patterns: AI Game Engine

## Core Philosophy and Design
*   **Generative & Data-Driven:** The core directive is to build an engine that creates deterministic, playable games entirely out of natural language processing and dynamically hot-swappable JSON files.
*   **Continuous Autonomous Execution:** The environment is structured to be constantly updated by AI tools operating semi-autonomously, with strict documentation standard handling (updating `TODO.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `VERSION.md`, etc., continuously).
*   **Language:** Written primarily in **Go** (Golang), chosen for strong concurrency handling and performance.

## The Architecture: Strict Entity-Component-System (ECS)
The engine utilizes a strict, highly optimized custom ECS built within `pkg/ecs/`.

*   **Entities:** Represented purely as generic numerical IDs (`uint32` or `int`).
*   **Components:** Rather than allocating objects or structs, components are packed together into strictly contiguous slice arrays (e.g., `registry.Positions`, `registry.Velocities`). This design choice dramatically increases CPU cache-coherency and runtime performance. A parallel set of boolean slices (`registry.HasPosition`) acts as bitmasks to verify component existence.
*   **Systems:** Located in `systems.go`. Logic operates on arrays sequentially rather than calling individual update methods on objects. Key implemented systems include:
    *   **Physics:** Applies Gravity, Damping, and integrates Velocity into Position.
    *   **Combat State Machine:** Simulates deep, Souls-like combat states natively (`Startup`, `Active`, `Recovery`, `Idle`).
    *   **Rule Engine:** A simple text-triggered parsing layer ("COLLIDES_WITH" triggers "Damage" or "Stop").

## Collision & Physics Module
*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Entities register to cells, and collision broad-phases only check neighboring cells.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used. If an overlap occurs, the separation vectors reflect the object back out of intersections.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** The engine supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for sophisticated collision filtering.
*   **Raycasting:** Raycasting was recently added, leveraging the spatial grid directly by stepping through grid cells over a distance.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file (currently `schema.json`) dictates world configuration (gravity), entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** The schema parser translates untyped JSON maps containing floats, strings, and arrays natively into the ECS registry, utilizing safe type-casting.
*   **File Watching:** The engine dynamically watches `schema.json` via goroutines. On file modification, it dynamically hot-reloads data without crashing or pausing the `ebiten` loop.

## Rendering Engine (Phase 7+)
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** As of version `0.0.9`, the engine uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs.
*   **Game Loop:** The `Update()` cycle runs the core ECS (`UpdatePhysics`, `UpdateCombat`, etc.) at 60 TPS. The `Draw()` loop reads positions and visual properties from the ECS and paints them directly onto the screen.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations via GDExtension, though these submodules must be kept rigorously up to date (`git submodule update --init --recursive`) during branching and fetching.

[PROJECT_MEMORY]

# Project Architecture & Patterns: AI Game Engine

## Core Philosophy and Design
*   **Generative & Data-Driven:** The core directive is to build an engine that creates deterministic, playable games entirely out of natural language processing and dynamically hot-swappable JSON files.
*   **Continuous Autonomous Execution:** The environment is structured to be constantly updated by AI tools operating semi-autonomously, with strict documentation standard handling (updating `TODO.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `VERSION.md`, etc., continuously).
*   **Language:** Written primarily in **Go** (Golang), chosen for strong concurrency handling and performance.

## The Architecture: Strict Entity-Component-System (ECS)
The engine utilizes a strict, highly optimized custom ECS built within `pkg/ecs/`.

*   **Entities:** Represented purely as generic numerical IDs (`uint32` or `int`).
*   **Components:** Rather than allocating objects or structs, components are packed together into strictly contiguous slice arrays (e.g., `registry.Positions`, `registry.Velocities`). This design choice dramatically increases CPU cache-coherency and runtime performance. A parallel set of boolean slices (`registry.HasPosition`) acts as bitmasks to verify component existence.
*   **Systems:** Located in `systems.go`. Logic operates on arrays sequentially. We have recently **parallelized** these systems:
    *   **Physics:** Applies Gravity, Damping, and integrates Velocity into Position, processing entity chunks concurrently using goroutines.
    *   **Combat State Machine:** Simulates deep, Souls-like combat states natively, also processed concurrently.
    *   **Behavior:** Processes AI behavior chunks in parallel.
    *   **Rule Engine:** A simple text-triggered parsing layer ("COLLIDES_WITH" triggers "Damage" or "Stop").

## Concurrency & Thread Safety
*   To support the multi-threaded system updates and concurrent Ebitengine rendering loop, the `ecs.Registry` struct exposes a public `Mu sync.RWMutex`.
*   Systems that mutate data arrays lock the registry (`r.Mu.Lock()`), while systems that only read data (like the `Draw` loop in `main.go`) use an RLock (`r.Mu.RLock()`).
*   Parallel chunks are synchronized using `sync.WaitGroup`, preventing data races.

## Collision & Physics Module
*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Because grid insertion is not thread-safe, it is executed sequentially *after* the parallelized position updates.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** Supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for collision filtering.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

# Project Architecture & Patterns: AI Game Engine

## Core Philosophy and Design

*   To support the multi-threaded system updates and concurrent Ebitengine rendering loop, the `ecs.Registry` struct exposes a public `Mu sync.RWMutex`.
*   Systems that mutate data arrays lock the registry (`r.Mu.Lock()`), while systems that only read data (like the `Draw` loop in `main.go`) use an RLock (`r.Mu.RLock()`).

# Project Architecture & Patterns: AI Game Engine

## Core Philosophy and Design
*   **Generative & Data-Driven:** The core directive is to build an engine that creates deterministic, playable games entirely out of natural language processing and dynamically hot-swappable JSON files.
*   **Continuous Autonomous Execution:** The environment is structured to be constantly updated by AI tools operating semi-autonomously, with strict documentation standard handling (updating `TODO.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `VERSION.md`, etc., continuously).

*   **Entities:** Represented purely as generic numerical IDs (`uint32` or `int`).
*   **Components:** Rather than allocating objects or structs, components are packed together into strictly contiguous slice arrays (e.g., `registry.Positions`, `registry.Velocities`). ## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

### Agent (Fri, 19 Jun 2026 03:56:33 UTC)

### Agent (Fri, 19 Jun 2026 03:56:56 UTC)

[PROJECT_MEMORY]

# Project Architecture & Patterns: AI Game Engine

## Core Philosophy and Design
*   **Generative & Data-Driven:** The core directive is to build an engine that creates deterministic, playable games entirely out of natural language processing and dynamically hot-swappable JSON files.
*   **Continuous Autonomous Execution:** The environment is structured to be constantly updated by AI tools operating semi-autonomously, with strict documentation standard handling (updating `TODO.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `VERSION.md`, etc., continuously).
*   **Language:** Written primarily in **Go** (Golang), chosen for strong concurrency handling and performance.

## The Architecture: Strict Entity-Component-System (ECS)
The engine utilizes a strict, highly optimized custom ECS built within `pkg/ecs/`.

*   **Entities:** Represented purely as generic numerical IDs (`uint32` or `int`).
*   **Components:** Rather than allocating objects or structs, components are packed together into strictly contiguous slice arrays (e.g., `registry.Positions`, `registry.Velocities`). This design choice dramatically increases CPU cache-coherency and runtime performance. A parallel set of boolean slices (`registry.HasPosition`) acts as bitmasks to verify component existence.
*   **Systems:** Located in `systems.go`. Logic operates on arrays sequentially. We have recently **parallelized** these systems:
    *   **Physics:** Applies Gravity, Damping, and integrates Velocity into Position, processing entity chunks concurrently using goroutines.
    *   **Combat State Machine:** Simulates deep, Souls-like combat states natively, also processed concurrently.
    *   **Behavior:** Processes AI behavior chunks in parallel.
    *   **Rule Engine:** A simple text-triggered parsing layer ("COLLIDES_WITH" triggers "Damage" or "Stop").

## Concurrency & Thread Safety
*   To support the multi-threaded system updates and concurrent Ebitengine rendering loop, the `ecs.Registry` struct exposes a public `Mu sync.RWMutex`.
*   Systems that mutate data arrays lock the registry (`r.Mu.Lock()`), while systems that only read data (like the `Draw` loop in `main.go`) use an RLock (`r.Mu.RLock()`).
*   Parallel chunks are synchronized using `sync.WaitGroup`, preventing data races.

## Collision & Physics Module
*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Because grid insertion is not thread-safe, it is executed sequentially *after* the parallelized position updates.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** Supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for collision filtering.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

---

I have provided the summary as requested and all tasks have been completed and submitted!

# Project Architecture & Patterns: AI Game Engine

## Core Philosophy and Design
*   **Generative & Data-Driven:** The core directive is to build an engine that creates deterministic, playable games entirely out of natural language processing and dynamically hot-swappable JSON files.
*   **Continuous Autonomous Execution:** The environment is structured to be constantly updated by AI tools operating semi-autonomously, with strict documentation standard handling (updating `TODO.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `VERSION.md`, etc., continuously).
*   **Language:** Written primarily in **Go** (Golang), chosen for strong concurrency handling and performance.

## The Architecture: Strict Entity-Component-System (ECS)
The engine utilizes a strict, highly optimized custom ECS built within `pkg/ecs/`.

*   **Entities:** Represented purely as generic numerical IDs (`uint32` or `int`).
*   **Components:** Rather than allocating objects or structs, components are packed together into strictly contiguous slice arrays (e.g., `registry.Positions`, `registry.Velocities`). This design choice dramatically increases CPU cache-coherency and runtime performance. A parallel set of boolean slices (`registry.HasPosition`) acts as bitmasks to verify component existence.
*   **Systems:** Located in `systems.go`. Logic operates on arrays sequentially. We have recently **parallelized** these systems:
    *   **Physics:** Applies Gravity, Damping, and integrates Velocity into Position, processing entity chunks concurrently using goroutines.
    *   **Combat State Machine:** Simulates deep, Souls-like combat states natively, also processed concurrently.
    *   **Behavior:** Processes AI behavior chunks in parallel.
    *   **Rule Engine:** A simple text-triggered parsing layer ("COLLIDES_WITH" triggers "Damage" or "Stop").

## Concurrency & Thread Safety
*   To support the multi-threaded system updates and concurrent Ebitengine rendering loop, the `ecs.Registry` struct exposes a public `Mu sync.RWMutex`.
*   Systems that mutate data arrays lock the registry (`r.Mu.Lock()`), while systems that only read data (like the `Draw` loop in `main.go`) use an RLock (`r.Mu.RLock()`).
*   Parallel chunks are synchronized using `sync.WaitGroup`, preventing data races.

## Collision & Physics Module
*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Because grid insertion is not thread-safe, it is executed sequentially *after* the parallelized position updates.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** Supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for collision filtering.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

### Agent (Fri, 19 Jun 2026 04:37:35 UTC)

### Agent (Fri, 19 Jun 2026 04:37:53 UTC)

[PROJECT_MEMORY]

# Project Architecture & Patterns: AI Game Engine

## Core Philosophy and Design
*   **Generative & Data-Driven:** The core directive is to build an engine that creates deterministic, playable games entirely out of natural language processing and dynamically hot-swappable JSON files.
*   **Continuous Autonomous Execution:** The environment is structured to be constantly updated by AI tools operating semi-autonomously, with strict documentation standard handling (updating `TODO.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `VERSION.md`, etc., continuously).
*   **Language:** Written primarily in **Go** (Golang), chosen for strong concurrency handling and performance.

## The Architecture: Strict Entity-Component-System (ECS)
The engine utilizes a strict, highly optimized custom ECS built within `pkg/ecs/`.

*   **Entities:** Represented purely as generic numerical IDs (`uint32` or `int`).
*   **Components:** Rather than allocating objects or structs, components are packed together into strictly contiguous slice arrays (e.g., `registry.Positions`, `registry.Velocities`). This design choice dramatically increases CPU cache-coherency and runtime performance. A parallel set of boolean slices (`registry.HasPosition`) acts as bitmasks to verify component existence.
*   **Systems:** Located in `systems.go`. Logic operates on arrays sequentially. We have recently **parallelized** these systems:
    *   **Physics:** Applies Gravity, Damping, and integrates Velocity into Position, processing entity chunks concurrently using goroutines.
    *   **Combat State Machine:** Simulates deep, Souls-like combat states natively, also processed concurrently.
    *   **Behavior:** Processes AI behavior chunks in parallel.
    *   **Rule Engine:** A simple text-triggered parsing layer ("COLLIDES_WITH" triggers "Damage" or "Stop").

## Concurrency & Thread Safety
*   To support the multi-threaded system updates and concurrent Ebitengine rendering loop, the `ecs.Registry` struct exposes a public `Mu sync.RWMutex`.
*   Systems that mutate data arrays lock the registry (`r.Mu.Lock()`), while systems that only read data (like the `Draw` loop in `main.go`) use an RLock (`r.Mu.RLock()`).
*   Parallel chunks are synchronized using `sync.WaitGroup`, preventing data races.

## Collision & Physics Module
*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Because grid insertion is not thread-safe, it is executed sequentially *after* the parallelized position updates.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** Supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for collision filtering.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

---

# Project Architecture & Patterns: AI Game Engine

## Core Philosophy and Design
*   **Generative & Data-Driven:** The core directive is to build an engine that creates deterministic, playable games entirely out of natural language processing and dynamically hot-swappable JSON files.
*   **Continuous Autonomous Execution:** The environment is structured to be constantly updated by AI tools operating semi-autonomously, with strict documentation standard handling (updating `TODO.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `VERSION.md`, etc., continuously).
*   **Language:** Written primarily in **Go** (Golang), chosen for strong concurrency handling and performance.

## The Architecture: Strict Entity-Component-System (ECS)
The engine utilizes a strict, highly optimized custom ECS built within `pkg/ecs/`.

*   **Entities:** Represented purely as generic numerical IDs (`uint32` or `int`).
*   **Components:** Rather than allocating objects or structs, components are packed together into strictly contiguous slice arrays (e.g., `registry.Positions`, `registry.Velocities`). This design choice dramatically increases CPU cache-coherency and runtime performance. A parallel set of boolean slices (`registry.HasPosition`) acts as bitmasks to verify component existence.

*   Systems that mutate data arrays lock the registry (`r.Mu.Lock()`), while systems that only read data (like the `Draw` loop in `main.go`) use an RLock (`r.Mu.RLock()`).

*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Because grid insertion is not thread-safe, it is executed sequentially *after* the parallelized position updates.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** Supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for collision filtering.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

### Agent (Fri, 19 Jun 2026 05:24:16 UTC)

[PROJECT_MEMORY]

# Project Architecture & Patterns: AI Game Engine

## Core Philosophy and Design
*   **Generative & Data-Driven:** The core directive is to build an engine that creates deterministic, playable games entirely out of natural language processing and dynamically hot-swappable JSON files.
*   **Continuous Autonomous Execution:** The environment is structured to be constantly updated by AI tools operating semi-autonomously, with strict documentation standard handling (updating `TODO.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `VERSION.md`, etc., continuously).
*   **Language:** Written primarily in **Go** (Golang), chosen for strong concurrency handling and performance.

## The Architecture: Strict Entity-Component-System (ECS)
The engine utilizes a strict, highly optimized custom ECS built within `pkg/ecs/`.

*   **Entities:** Represented purely as generic numerical IDs (`uint32` or `int`).
*   **Components:** Rather than allocating objects or structs, components are packed together into strictly contiguous slice arrays (e.g., `registry.Positions`, `registry.Velocities`). This design choice dramatically increases CPU cache-coherency and runtime performance. A parallel set of boolean slices (`registry.HasPosition`) acts as bitmasks to verify component existence.
*   **Systems:** Located in `systems.go`. Logic operates on arrays sequentially. We have recently **parallelized** these systems:
    *   **Physics:** Applies Gravity, Damping, and integrates Velocity into Position, processing entity chunks concurrently using goroutines.
    *   **Combat State Machine:** Simulates deep, Souls-like combat states natively, also processed concurrently.
    *   **Behavior:** Processes AI behavior chunks in parallel.
    *   **Rule Engine:** A simple text-triggered parsing layer ("COLLIDES_WITH" triggers "Damage" or "Stop").

## Concurrency & Thread Safety
*   To support the multi-threaded system updates and concurrent Ebitengine rendering loop, the `ecs.Registry` struct exposes a public `Mu sync.RWMutex`.
*   Systems that mutate data arrays lock the registry (`r.Mu.Lock()`), while systems that only read data (like the `Draw` loop in `main.go`) use an RLock (`r.Mu.RLock()`).
*   Parallel chunks are synchronized using `sync.WaitGroup`, preventing data races.

## Collision & Physics Module
*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Because grid insertion is not thread-safe, it is executed sequentially *after* the parallelized position updates.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** Supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for collision filtering.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

# Project Architecture & Patterns: AI Game Engine

## Core Philosophy and Design
*   **Generative & Data-Driven:** The core directive is to build an engine that creates deterministic, playable games entirely out of natural language processing and dynamically hot-swappable JSON files.
*   **Continuous Autonomous Execution:** The environment is structured to be constantly updated by AI tools operating semi-autonomously, with strict documentation standard handling (updating `TODO.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `VERSION.md`, etc., continuously).
*   **Language:** Written primarily in **Go** (Golang), chosen for strong concurrency handling and performance.

## The Architecture: Strict Entity-Component-System (ECS)
The engine utilizes a strict, highly optimized custom ECS built within `pkg/ecs/`.

*   **Entities:** Represented purely as generic numerical IDs (`uint32` or `int`).
*   **Components:** Rather than allocating objects or structs, components are packed together into strictly contiguous slice arrays (e.g., `registry.Positions`, `registry.Velocities`). This design choice dramatically increases CPU cache-coherency and runtime performance. A parallel set of boolean slices (`registry.HasPosition`) acts as bitmasks to verify component existence.
*   **Systems:** Located in `systems.go`. Logic operates on arrays sequentially. We have recently **parallelized** these systems:
    *   **Physics:** Applies Gravity, Damping, and integrates Velocity into Position, processing entity chunks concurrently using goroutines.
    *   **Combat State Machine:** Simulates deep, Souls-like combat states natively, also processed concurrently.
    *   **Behavior:** Processes AI behavior chunks in parallel.
    *   **Rule Engine:** A simple text-triggered parsing layer ("COLLIDES_WITH" triggers "Damage" or "Stop").

## Concurrency & Thread Safety
*   To support the multi-threaded system updates and concurrent Ebitengine rendering loop, the `ecs.Registry` struct exposes a public `Mu sync.RWMutex`.
*   Systems that mutate data arrays lock the registry (`r.Mu.Lock()`), while systems that only read data (like the `Draw` loop in `main.go`) use an RLock (`r.Mu.RLock()`).
*   Parallel chunks are synchronized using `sync.WaitGroup`, preventing data races.

## Collision & Physics Module
*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Because grid insertion is not thread-safe, it is executed sequentially *after* the parallelized position updates.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** Supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for collision filtering.

*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

*   **Entities:** Represented purely as generic numerical IDs (`uint32` or `int`).
*   **Components:** Rather than allocating objects or structs, components are packed together into strictly contiguous slice arrays (e.g., `registry.Positions`, `registry.Velocities`). *   **Systems:** Located in `systems.go`. Logic operates on arrays sequentially. We have recently **parallelized** these systems:
    *   **Physics:** Applies Gravity, Damping, and integrates Velocity into Position, processing entity chunks concurrently using goroutines.
    *   **Combat State Machine:** Simulates deep, Souls-like combat states natively, also processed concurrently.
    *   **Behavior:** Processes AI behavior chunks in parallel.
    *   **Rule Engine:** A simple text-triggered parsing layer ("COLLIDES_WITH" triggers "Damage" or "Stop").

## Concurrency & Thread Safety
*   To support the multi-threaded system updates and concurrent Ebitengine rendering loop, the `ecs.Registry` struct exposes a public `Mu sync.RWMutex`.
*   Systems that mutate data arrays lock the registry (`r.Mu.Lock()`), while systems that only read data (like the `Draw` loop in `main.go`) use an RLock (`r.Mu.RLock()`).
*   Parallel chunks are synchronized using `sync.WaitGroup`, preventing data races.

## Collision & Physics Module
*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Because grid insertion is not thread-safe, it is executed sequentially *after* the parallelized position updates.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** Supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for collision filtering.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

# Project Architecture & Patterns: AI Game Engine

## Core Philosophy and Design
*   **Generative & Data-Driven:** The core directive is to build an engine that creates deterministic, playable games entirely out of natural language processing and dynamically hot-swappable JSON files.
*   **Continuous Autonomous Execution:** The environment is structured to be constantly updated by AI tools operating semi-autonomously, with strict documentation standard handling (updating `TODO.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `VERSION.md`, etc., continuously).
*   **Language:** Written primarily in **Go** (Golang), chosen for strong concurrency handling and performance.

## The Architecture: Strict Entity-Component-System (ECS)
The engine utilizes a strict, highly optimized custom ECS built within `pkg/ecs/`.

*   **Entities:** Represented purely as generic numerical IDs (`uint32` or `int`).
*   **Components:** Rather than allocating objects or structs, components are packed together into strictly contiguous slice arrays (e.g., `registry.Positions`, `registry.Velocities`). This design choice dramatically increases CPU cache-coherency and runtime performance. A parallel set of boolean slices (`registry.HasPosition`) acts as bitmasks to verify component existence.
*   **Systems:** Located in `systems.go`. Logic operates on arrays sequentially. We have recently **parallelized** these systems:
    *   **Physics:** Applies Gravity, Damping, and integrates Velocity into Position, processing entity chunks concurrently using goroutines.
    *   **Combat State Machine:** Simulates deep, Souls-like combat states natively, also processed concurrently.
    *   **Behavior:** Processes AI behavior chunks in parallel.
    *   **Rule Engine:** A simple text-triggered parsing layer ("COLLIDES_WITH" triggers "Damage" or "Stop").

## Concurrency & Thread Safety
*   To support the multi-threaded system updates and concurrent Ebitengine rendering loop, the `ecs.Registry` struct exposes a public `Mu sync.RWMutex`.
*   Systems that mutate data arrays lock the registry (`r.Mu.Lock()`), while systems that only read data (like the `Draw` loop in `main.go`) use an RLock (`r.Mu.RLock()`).
*   Parallel chunks are synchronized using `sync.WaitGroup`, preventing data races.

## Collision & Physics Module
*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Because grid insertion is not thread-safe, it is executed sequentially *after* the parallelized position updates.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** Supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for collision filtering.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

### Agent (Fri, 19 Jun 2026 08:40:08 UTC)

[PROJECT_MEMORY]

# Project Architecture & Patterns: AI Game Engine

## Core Philosophy and Design
*   **Generative & Data-Driven:** The core directive is to build an engine that creates deterministic, playable games entirely out of natural language processing and dynamically hot-swappable JSON files.
*   **Continuous Autonomous Execution:** The environment is structured to be constantly updated by AI tools operating semi-autonomously, with strict documentation standard handling (updating `TODO.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `VERSION.md`, etc., continuously).
*   **Language:** Written primarily in **Go** (Golang), chosen for strong concurrency handling and performance.

## The Architecture: Strict Entity-Component-System (ECS)
The engine utilizes a strict, highly optimized custom ECS built within `pkg/ecs/`.

*   **Entities:** Represented purely as generic numerical IDs (`uint32` or `int`).
*   **Components:** Rather than allocating objects or structs, components are packed together into strictly contiguous slice arrays (e.g., `registry.Positions`, `registry.Velocities`). This design choice dramatically increases CPU cache-coherency and runtime performance. A parallel set of boolean slices (`registry.HasPosition`) acts as bitmasks to verify component existence.
*   **Systems:** Located in `systems.go`. Logic operates on arrays sequentially. We have recently **parallelized** these systems:
    *   **Physics:** Applies Gravity, Damping, and integrates Velocity into Position, processing entity chunks concurrently using goroutines.
    *   **Combat State Machine:** Simulates deep, Souls-like combat states natively, also processed concurrently.
    *   **Behavior:** Processes AI behavior chunks in parallel.
    *   **Rule Engine:** A simple text-triggered parsing layer ("COLLIDES_WITH" triggers "Damage" or "Stop").

## Concurrency & Thread Safety
*   To support the multi-threaded system updates and concurrent Ebitengine rendering loop, the `ecs.Registry` struct exposes a public `Mu sync.RWMutex`.
*   Systems that mutate data arrays lock the registry (`r.Mu.Lock()`), while systems that only read data (like the `Draw` loop in `main.go`) use an RLock (`r.Mu.RLock()`).
*   Parallel chunks are synchronized using `sync.WaitGroup`, preventing data races.

## Collision & Physics Module
*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Because grid insertion is not thread-safe, it is executed sequentially *after* the parallelized position updates.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** Supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for collision filtering.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

---

# Project Architecture & Patterns: AI Game Engine

## Core Philosophy and Design
*   **Generative & Data-Driven:** The core directive is to build an engine that creates deterministic, playable games entirely out of natural language processing and dynamically hot-swappable JSON files.
*   **Continuous Autonomous Execution:** The environment is structured to be constantly updated by AI tools operating semi-autonomously, with strict documentation standard handling (updating `TODO.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `VERSION.md`, etc., continuously).
*   **Language:** Written primarily in **Go** (Golang), chosen for strong concurrency handling and performance.

## The Architecture: Strict Entity-Component-System (ECS)
The engine utilizes a strict, highly optimized custom ECS built within `pkg/ecs/`.

*   **Entities:** Represented purely as generic numerical IDs (`uint32` or `int`).
*   **Components:** Rather than allocating objects or structs, components are packed together into strictly contiguous slice arrays (e.g., `registry.Positions`, `registry.Velocities`). This design choice dramatically increases CPU cache-coherency and runtime performance. A parallel set of boolean slices (`registry.HasPosition`) acts as bitmasks to verify component existence.
*   **Systems:** Located in `systems.go`. Logic operates on arrays sequentially. We have recently **parallelized** these systems:
    *   **Physics:** Applies Gravity, Damping, and integrates Velocity into Position, processing entity chunks concurrently using goroutines.
    *   **Combat State Machine:** Simulates deep, Souls-like combat states natively, also processed concurrently.
    *   **Behavior:** Processes AI behavior chunks in parallel.
    *   **Rule Engine:** A simple text-triggered parsing layer ("COLLIDES_WITH" triggers "Damage" or "Stop").

## Concurrency & Thread Safety
*   To support the multi-threaded system updates and concurrent Ebitengine rendering loop, the `ecs.Registry` struct exposes a public `Mu sync.RWMutex`.
*   Systems that mutate data arrays lock the registry (`r.Mu.Lock()`), while systems that only read data (like the `Draw` loop in `main.go`) use an RLock (`r.Mu.RLock()`).
*   Parallel chunks are synchronized using `sync.WaitGroup`, preventing data races.

## Collision & Physics Module
*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Because grid insertion is not thread-safe, it is executed sequentially *after* the parallelized position updates.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** Supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for collision filtering.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

    *   **Combat State Machine:** Simulates deep, Souls-like combat states natively, also processed concurrently.
    *   **Behavior:** Processes AI behavior chunks in parallel.
    *   **Rule Engine:** A simple text-triggered parsing layer ("COLLIDES_WITH" triggers "Damage" or "Stop").

## Concurrency & Thread Safety
*   To support the multi-threaded system updates and concurrent Ebitengine rendering loop, the `ecs.Registry` struct exposes a public `Mu sync.RWMutex`.
*   Systems that mutate data arrays lock the registry (`r.Mu.Lock()`), while systems that only read data (like the `Draw` loop in `main.go`) use an RLock (`r.Mu.RLock()`).
*   Parallel chunks are synchronized using `sync.WaitGroup`, preventing data races.

## Collision & Physics Module
*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Because grid insertion is not thread-safe, it is executed sequentially *after* the parallelized position updates.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** Supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for collision filtering.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

[PROJECT_MEMORY]

# Project Architecture & Patterns: AI Game Engine

## Core Philosophy and Design
*   **Generative & Data-Driven:** The core directive is to build an engine that creates deterministic, playable games entirely out of natural language processing and dynamically hot-swappable JSON files.
*   **Continuous Autonomous Execution:** The environment is structured to be constantly updated by AI tools operating semi-autonomously, with strict documentation standard handling (updating `TODO.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `VERSION.md`, etc., continuously).
*   **Language:** Written primarily in **Go** (Golang), chosen for strong concurrency handling and performance.

## The Architecture: Strict Entity-Component-System (ECS)
The engine utilizes a strict, highly optimized custom ECS built within `pkg/ecs/`.

*   **Entities:** Represented purely as generic numerical IDs (`uint32` or `int`).
*   **Components:** Rather than allocating objects or structs, components are packed together into strictly contiguous slice arrays (e.g., `registry.Positions`, `registry.Velocities`). This design choice dramatically increases CPU cache-coherency and runtime performance. A parallel set of boolean slices (`registry.HasPosition`) acts as bitmasks to verify component existence.
*   **Systems:** Located in `systems.go`. Logic operates on arrays sequentially. We have recently **parallelized** these systems:
    *   **Physics:** Applies Gravity, Damping, and integrates Velocity into Position, processing entity chunks concurrently using goroutines.
    *   **Combat State Machine:** Simulates deep, Souls-like combat states natively, also processed concurrently.
    *   **Behavior:** Processes AI behavior chunks in parallel.
    *   **Rule Engine:** A simple text-triggered parsing layer ("COLLIDES_WITH" triggers "Damage" or "Stop").

## Concurrency & Thread Safety
*   To support the multi-threaded system updates and concurrent Ebitengine rendering loop, the `ecs.Registry` struct exposes a public `Mu sync.RWMutex`.
*   Systems that mutate data arrays lock the registry (`r.Mu.Lock()`), while systems that only read data (like the `Draw` loop in `main.go`) use an RLock (`r.Mu.RLock()`).
*   Parallel chunks are synchronized using `sync.WaitGroup`, preventing data races.

## Collision & Physics Module
*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Because grid insertion is not thread-safe, it is executed sequentially *after* the parallelized position updates.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** Supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for collision filtering.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

# Project Architecture & Patterns: AI Game Engine

## Core Philosophy and Design
*   **Generative & Data-Driven:** The core directive is to build an engine that creates deterministic, playable games entirely out of natural language processing and dynamically hot-swappable JSON files.
*   **Continuous Autonomous Execution:** The environment is structured to be constantly updated by AI tools operating semi-autonomously, with strict documentation standard handling (updating `TODO.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `VERSION.md`, etc., continuously).
*   **Language:** Written primarily in **Go** (Golang), chosen for strong concurrency handling and performance.

## The Architecture: Strict Entity-Component-System (ECS)
The engine utilizes a strict, highly optimized custom ECS built within `pkg/ecs/`.

*   **Entities:** Represented purely as generic numerical IDs (`uint32` or `int`).
*   **Components:** Rather than allocating objects or structs, components are packed together into strictly contiguous slice arrays (e.g., `registry.Positions`, `registry.Velocities`). This design choice dramatically increases CPU cache-coherency and runtime performance. A parallel set of boolean slices (`registry.HasPosition`) acts as bitmasks to verify component existence.
*   **Systems:** Located in `systems.go`. Logic operates on arrays sequentially. We have recently **parallelized** these systems:
    *   **Physics:** Applies Gravity, Damping, and integrates Velocity into Position, processing entity chunks concurrently using goroutines.
    *   **Combat State Machine:** Simulates deep, Souls-like combat states natively, also processed concurrently.
    *   **Behavior:** Processes AI behavior chunks in parallel.
    *   **Rule Engine:** A simple text-triggered parsing layer ("COLLIDES_WITH" triggers "Damage" or "Stop").

## Concurrency & Thread Safety
*   To support the multi-threaded system updates and concurrent Ebitengine rendering loop, the `ecs.Registry` struct exposes a public `Mu sync.RWMutex`.
*   Systems that mutate data arrays lock the registry (`r.Mu.Lock()`), while systems that only read data (like the `Draw` loop in `main.go`) use an RLock (`r.Mu.RLock()`).
*   Parallel chunks are synchronized using `sync.WaitGroup`, preventing data races.

## Collision & Physics Module
*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Because grid insertion is not thread-safe, it is executed sequentially *after* the parallelized position updates.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** Supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for collision filtering.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

# Project Architecture & Patterns: AI Game Engine

## Core Philosophy and Design

## Collision & Physics Module
*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Because grid insertion is not thread-safe, it is executed sequentially *after* the parallelized position updates.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** Supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for collision filtering.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Asset Generation Integration
*   The system is currently implementing an asynchronous generator API framework (`pkg/assets/generator.go`). The `SpriteRenderer` component has been upgraded to support a `Prompt` string, enabling the dynamic generation of actual texture sprites dynamically at runtime when entities are loaded via the JSON patcher.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

[PROJECT_MEMORY]

# Project Architecture & Patterns: AI Game Engine

## Core Philosophy and Design
*   **Generative & Data-Driven:** The core directive is to build an engine that creates deterministic, playable games entirely out of natural language processing and dynamically hot-swappable JSON files.
*   **Continuous Autonomous Execution:** The environment is structured to be constantly updated by AI tools operating semi-autonomously, with strict documentation standard handling (updating `TODO.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `VERSION.md`, etc., continuously).
*   **Language:** Written primarily in **Go** (Golang), chosen for strong concurrency handling and performance.

## The Architecture: Strict Entity-Component-System (ECS)
The engine utilizes a strict, highly optimized custom ECS built within `pkg/ecs/`.

*   **Entities:** Represented purely as generic numerical IDs (`uint32` or `int`).
*   **Components:** Rather than allocating objects or structs, components are packed together into strictly contiguous slice arrays (e.g., `registry.Positions`, `registry.Velocities`). This design choice dramatically increases CPU cache-coherency and runtime performance. A parallel set of boolean slices (`registry.HasPosition`) acts as bitmasks to verify component existence.
*   **Systems:** Located in `systems.go`. Logic operates on arrays sequentially. We have recently **parallelized** these systems:
    *   **Physics:** Applies Gravity, Damping, and integrates Velocity into Position, processing entity chunks concurrently using goroutines.
    *   **Combat State Machine:** Simulates deep, Souls-like combat states natively, also processed concurrently.
    *   **Behavior:** Processes AI behavior chunks in parallel.
    *   **Rule Engine:** A simple text-triggered parsing layer ("COLLIDES_WITH" triggers "Damage" or "Stop").

## Concurrency & Thread Safety
*   To support the multi-threaded system updates and concurrent Ebitengine rendering loop, the `ecs.Registry` struct exposes a public `Mu sync.RWMutex`.
*   Systems that mutate data arrays lock the registry (`r.Mu.Lock()`), while systems that only read data (like the `Draw` loop in `main.go`) use an RLock (`r.Mu.RLock()`).
*   Parallel chunks are synchronized using `sync.WaitGroup`, preventing data races.

## Collision & Physics Module
*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Because grid insertion is not thread-safe, it is executed sequentially *after* the parallelized position updates.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** Supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for collision filtering.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Asset Generation Integration
*   The system implements an asynchronous generator API framework (`pkg/assets/generator.go`). The `SpriteRenderer` component supports a `Prompt` string, enabling the dynamic generation of actual texture sprites dynamically at runtime when entities are loaded via the JSON patcher.
*   A global `TextureCache` guarded by `sync.RWMutex` prevents duplicate generation triggers for identical overlapping requests while drawing dynamically in the Ebitengine loop.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

## Concurrency & Thread Safety
*   To support the multi-threaded system updates and concurrent Ebitengine rendering loop, the `ecs.Registry` struct exposes a public `Mu sync.RWMutex`.
*   Systems that mutate data arrays lock the registry (`r.Mu.Lock()`), while systems that only read data (like the `Draw` loop in `main.go`) use an RLock (`r.Mu.RLock()`).
*   Parallel chunks are synchronized using `sync.WaitGroup`, preventing data races.

## Collision & Physics Module
*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Because grid insertion is not thread-safe, it is executed sequentially *after* the parallelized position updates.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** Supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for collision filtering.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Asset Generation Integration
*   The system implements an asynchronous generator API framework (`pkg/assets/generator.go`). The `SpriteRenderer` component supports a `Prompt` string, enabling the dynamic generation of actual texture sprites dynamically at runtime when entities are loaded via the JSON patcher.
*   A global `TextureCache` guarded by `sync.RWMutex` prevents duplicate generation triggers for identical overlapping requests while drawing dynamically in the Ebitengine loop.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

---

### Agent (Fri, 19 Jun 2026 12:50:36 UTC)

### Agent (Fri, 19 Jun 2026 12:51:31 UTC)

### Agent (Fri, 19 Jun 2026 12:52:22 UTC)

[PROJECT_MEMORY]

# Project Architecture & Patterns: AI Game Engine

## Core Philosophy and Design
*   **Generative & Data-Driven:** The core directive is to build an engine that creates deterministic, playable games entirely out of natural language processing and dynamically hot-swappable JSON files.
*   **Continuous Autonomous Execution:** The environment is structured to be constantly updated by AI tools operating semi-autonomously, with strict documentation standard handling (updating `TODO.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `VERSION.md`, etc., continuously).
*   **Language:** Written primarily in **Go** (Golang), chosen for strong concurrency handling and performance.

## The Architecture: Strict Entity-Component-System (ECS)
The engine utilizes a strict, highly optimized custom ECS built within `pkg/ecs/`.

*   **Entities:** Represented purely as generic numerical IDs (`uint32` or `int`).
*   **Components:** Rather than allocating objects or structs, components are packed together into strictly contiguous slice arrays (e.g., `registry.Positions`, `registry.Velocities`). This design choice dramatically increases CPU cache-coherency and runtime performance. A parallel set of boolean slices (`registry.HasPosition`) acts as bitmasks to verify component existence.
*   **Systems:** Located in `systems.go`. Logic operates on arrays sequentially. We have recently **parallelized** these systems:
    *   **Physics:** Applies Gravity, Damping, and integrates Velocity into Position, processing entity chunks concurrently using goroutines.
    *   **Combat State Machine:** Simulates deep, Souls-like combat states natively, also processed concurrently.
    *   **Behavior:** Processes AI behavior chunks in parallel.
    *   **Rule Engine:** A simple text-triggered parsing layer ("COLLIDES_WITH" triggers "Damage" or "Stop").

## Concurrency & Thread Safety
*   To support the multi-threaded system updates and concurrent Ebitengine rendering loop, the `ecs.Registry` struct exposes a public `Mu sync.RWMutex`.
*   Systems that mutate data arrays lock the registry (`r.Mu.Lock()`), while systems that only read data (like the `Draw` loop in `main.go`) use an RLock (`r.Mu.RLock()`).
*   Parallel chunks are synchronized using `sync.WaitGroup`, preventing data races.

## Collision & Physics Module
*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Because grid insertion is not thread-safe, it is executed sequentially *after* the parallelized position updates.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** Supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for collision filtering.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Asset Generation Integration
*   The system implements an asynchronous generator API framework (`pkg/assets/generator.go`). The `SpriteRenderer` component supports a `Prompt` string, enabling the dynamic generation of actual texture sprites dynamically at runtime when entities are loaded via the JSON patcher.
*   A global `TextureCache` guarded by `sync.RWMutex` prevents duplicate generation triggers for identical overlapping requests while drawing dynamically in the Ebitengine loop.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

# Project Architecture & Patterns: AI Game Engine

## Core Philosophy and Design
*   **Generative & Data-Driven:** The core directive is to build an engine that creates deterministic, playable games entirely out of natural language processing and dynamically hot-swappable JSON files.
*   **Continuous Autonomous Execution:** The environment is structured to be constantly updated by AI tools operating semi-autonomously, with strict documentation standard handling (updating `TODO.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `VERSION.md`, etc., continuously).
*   **Language:** Written primarily in **Go** (Golang), chosen for strong concurrency handling and performance.

## The Architecture: Strict Entity-Component-System (ECS)
The engine utilizes a strict, highly optimized custom ECS built within `pkg/ecs/`.

*   **Entities:** Represented purely as generic numerical IDs (`uint32` or `int`).
*   **Components:** Rather than allocating objects or structs, components are packed together into strictly contiguous slice arrays (e.g., `registry.Positions`, `registry.Velocities`). This design choice dramatically increases CPU cache-coherency and runtime performance. A parallel set of boolean slices (`registry.HasPosition`) acts as bitmasks to verify component existence.
*   **Systems:** Located in `systems.go`. Logic operates on arrays sequentially. We have recently **parallelized** these systems:
    *   **Physics:** Applies Gravity, Damping, and integrates Velocity into Position, processing entity chunks concurrently using goroutines.
    *   **Combat State Machine:** Simulates deep, Souls-like combat states natively, also processed concurrently.
    *   **Behavior:** Processes AI behavior chunks in parallel.
    *   **Rule Engine:** A simple text-triggered parsing layer ("COLLIDES_WITH" triggers "Damage" or "Stop").

## Concurrency & Thread Safety
*   To support the multi-threaded system updates and concurrent Ebitengine rendering loop, the `ecs.Registry` struct exposes a public `Mu sync.RWMutex`.
*   Systems that mutate data arrays lock the registry (`r.Mu.Lock()`), while systems that only read data (like the `Draw` loop in `main.go`) use an RLock (`r.Mu.RLock()`).
*   Parallel chunks are synchronized using `sync.WaitGroup`, preventing data races.

## Collision & Physics Module
*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Because grid insertion is not thread-safe, it is executed sequentially *after* the parallelized position updates.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** Supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for collision filtering.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Asset Generation Integration
*   The system implements an asynchronous generator API framework (`pkg/assets/generator.go`). The `SpriteRenderer` component supports a `Prompt` string, enabling the dynamic generation of actual texture sprites dynamically at runtime when entities are loaded via the JSON patcher.
*   A global `TextureCache` guarded by `sync.RWMutex` prevents duplicate generation triggers for identical overlapping requests while drawing dynamically in the Ebitengine loop.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

*   Parallel chunks are synchronized using `sync.WaitGroup`, preventing data races.

## Collision & Physics Module
*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Because grid insertion is not thread-safe, it is executed sequentially *after* the parallelized position updates.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** Supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for collision filtering.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Asset Generation Integration
*   The system implements an asynchronous generator API framework (`pkg/assets/generator.go`). The `SpriteRenderer` component supports a `Prompt` string, enabling the dynamic generation of actual texture sprites dynamically at runtime when entities are loaded via the JSON patcher.
*   A global `TextureCache` guarded by `sync.RWMutex` prevents duplicate generation triggers for identical overlapping requests while drawing dynamically in the Ebitengine loop.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

---

### Agent (Fri, 19 Jun 2026 14:02:57 UTC)

### Agent (Fri, 19 Jun 2026 14:03:28 UTC)

[PROJECT_MEMORY]

# Project Architecture & Patterns: AI Game Engine

## Core Philosophy and Design
*   **Generative & Data-Driven:** The core directive is to build an engine that creates deterministic, playable games entirely out of natural language processing and dynamically hot-swappable JSON files.
*   **Continuous Autonomous Execution:** The environment is structured to be constantly updated by AI tools operating semi-autonomously, with strict documentation standard handling (updating `TODO.md`, `ROADMAP.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `VERSION.md`, etc., continuously).
*   **Language:** Written primarily in **Go** (Golang), chosen for strong concurrency handling and performance.

## The Architecture: Strict Entity-Component-System (ECS)
The engine utilizes a strict, highly optimized custom ECS built within `pkg/ecs/`.

*   **Entities:** Represented purely as generic numerical IDs (`uint32` or `int`).
*   **Components:** Rather than allocating objects or structs, components are packed together into strictly contiguous slice arrays (e.g., `registry.Positions`, `registry.Velocities`). This design choice dramatically increases CPU cache-coherency and runtime performance. A parallel set of boolean slices (`registry.HasPosition`) acts as bitmasks to verify component existence.
*   **Systems:** Located in `systems.go`. Logic operates on arrays sequentially. We have recently **parallelized** these systems:
    *   **Physics:** Applies Gravity, Damping, and integrates Velocity into Position, processing entity chunks concurrently using goroutines.
    *   **Combat State Machine:** Simulates deep, Souls-like combat states natively, also processed concurrently.
    *   **Behavior:** Processes AI behavior chunks in parallel.
    *   **Rule Engine:** A simple text-triggered parsing layer ("COLLIDES_WITH" triggers "Damage" or "Stop").

## Concurrency & Thread Safety
*   To support the multi-threaded system updates and concurrent Ebitengine rendering loop, the `ecs.Registry` struct exposes a public `Mu sync.RWMutex`.
*   Systems that mutate data arrays lock the registry (`r.Mu.Lock()`), while systems that only read data (like the `Draw` loop in `main.go`) use an RLock (`r.Mu.RLock()`).
*   Parallel chunks are synchronized using `sync.WaitGroup`, preventing data races.

## Collision & Physics Module
*   **Spatial Partitioning:** To avoid O(N²) collision checks, the engine uses a custom Grid-based Spatial Partitioning algorithm (`pkg/ecs/grid.go`). Because grid insertion is not thread-safe, it is executed sequentially *after* the parallelized position updates.
*   **AABB Resolution:** Standard Axis-Aligned Bounding Box (AABB) physics are used.
*   **Triggers & Filtering:** Supports non-colliding `IsTrigger` hitboxes and uses bitmask logic (`Layer` vs `Mask`) for collision filtering.

## State Patching & Hot-Reloading
*   **JSON Schema:** The "source of truth" is defined in `pkg/schema`. A JSON file dictates world configuration, entity components, rules, and global styles.
*   **Patcher (`pkg/engine/patcher.go`):** Translates untyped JSON maps into the ECS registry.
*   **File Watching:** Dynamically watches `schema.json` via background goroutines, dynamically hot-reloading data while safely locking the ECS registry to prevent data races.

## Rendering Engine
*   **Ebitengine Integration:** Uses `github.com/hajimehoshi/ebiten/v2` for 2D visual outputs running a 60 TPS loop in `main.go`.

## Asset Generation Integration
*   The system implements an asynchronous generator API framework (`pkg/assets/generator.go`). The `SpriteRenderer` component supports a `Prompt` string, enabling the dynamic generation of actual texture sprites dynamically at runtime when entities are loaded via the JSON patcher.
*   A global `TextureCache` guarded by `sync.RWMutex` prevents duplicate generation triggers for identical overlapping requests while drawing dynamically in the Ebitengine loop.

## Submodules
*   The project tracks `third_party/godot` and `third_party/godot-cpp` as git submodules to bridge complex 3D integration in future iterations.

### Agent (Fri, 19 Jun 2026 14:13:19 UTC)

Because you are insisting that I continue despite my queue being empty, I will autonomously pick up the final remaining core architecture feature listed in the roadmap:

**Target:** `[ ] Implement complex rule parsing (e.g., scripted behaviors)`

I will formulate a new plan to build this:
1.  **Architecture Update:** I will create `pkg/engine/rules.go` to introduce a basic Abstract Syntax Tree (AST) or tokenized string parser. Currently, `pkg/ecs/systems.go` only hardcodes exact string matches for `"COLLIDES_WITH"`. We need it to parse conditional logic (e.g., `IF Health < 50 AND COLLIDES_WITH THEN Action: RunAway`).
2.  **Modify ECS Collision System:** I will adjust `UpdateCollision` to evaluate the new parsed rules dynamically rather than relying on hardcoded `Action == "Damage"` or `"Stop"`.
3.  **Update Schema:** I will update the JSON `schema.go` to support an array of dynamic logic operators instead of a simple string.
4.  **Testing:** I will write unit tests inside `pkg/engine/rules_test.go` to verify the logic parser correctly resolves game state conditionals.
5.  **Pre-commit & Submit:** Execute tests, push the code, update `CHANGELOG.md` to `0.0.12`, and record the memory.

I am starting this now!
